‚óŹ game.draw_ball eliminated. No procs in main.arche or game.arche ‚ÄĒ the rpg's
  own code is fully proc-free, and render draws each queried entity directly via
  gfx.circle. Still renders (3065 px).

  Where the rpg stands

  Proc-free: the app (main.arche) and the game device (game.arche) ‚ÄĒ all
  systems, one map, a query, consts. Zero procs.

  The only procs left are the gfx device's C-boundary wrappers ‚ÄĒ gfx.open /
  gfx.circle / gfx.clear / gfx.present / gfx.poll. And the only mutable file
  global is win. These are the same thing: the gfx-device migration. Both fall
  when the gfx device:
  - owns the window C-side (drops the win handle from its API ‚Üí win disappears
  from the app), and
  - exposes drawing as funcs over the framebuffer + the present/poll externs (so
  circle/clear stop being procs).

  So the rpg has been driven as far as it can go without touching the gfx
  device. The remaining proc‚Üíproc and the lone win global both terminate at that
  one migration ‚ÄĒ it's now the single, well-scoped next step rather than
  scattered cleanup.

  That migration touches 3 C backends (x11/wayland/headless) + gfx.arche, and I
  can only run the headless one. Want me to do it headless-first (convert the
  headless backend + gfx.arche to a C-side window with no handle, leave
  x11/wayland as a mechanical mirror to verify on a display), and prove the rpg
  fully proc-free + win-free headless?

  ‚éŅ ¬†Lint warning [proc_could_be_func] at line 13, col 1: proc 'os.argv' ha

‚ĚĮ the system query also doesn't make sense at all. wtf is pos.x if pos is a     
  column?                                                                       

‚óŹ You're right. Let me answer all three of your critiques honestly, because
  they're the same problem wearing three hats ‚ÄĒ and stop building on the broken
  model.

  "wtf is pos.x if pos is a column?"

  It's incoherent, and you caught a real leak. In the columnar model pos is a
  column and pos.x is its x sub-column. map gets away with vel.x -= (pos.x - 
  CENTER_X)/STIFFNESS because that's a whole-sub-column data-parallel op ‚ÄĒ there
  is no "current row."

  But system(query{pos,color}) has the body gfx.circle(win, pos.x, pos.y, color)
  ‚ÄĒ here pos.x must be one scalar, which only exists if there's a current 
  entity. A columnar query{} has no current entity. I faked one: system(query)
  secretly wraps the body in a hidden row loop + row index so pos.x lowers to
  pos_x[row]. So pos.x-as-a-scalar is codegen magic, not a real meaning. The
  surface says "column," the body assumes "row." That's the contradiction.

  "why is step called from the super-system pace, not the scheduler?"

  Same disease. core.arche:84 says the scheduler reads no program state ‚ÄĒ so the
  fixed-timestep drain (while bank >= DT, a runtime condition) can't live
  there. I shoved it into pace, which then does run game.step ‚ÄĒ a system 
  orchestrating another system. Orchestration smuggled into a system body,
  exactly the "super-system" you keep rejecting.

  The unifying diagnosis

  Both are systems overreaching ‚ÄĒ doing iteration and orchestration that aren't
  theirs. I reached for system every time because it was the one effectful tool,
  and bolted on whatever it lacked (a row loop; a dispatch call). The clean
  split:

‚óŹ Stopping. And yes ‚ÄĒ you caught the right thing: my Window.handle[0] everywhere
  is exactly the hand-indexing you're describing. Here's my honest take on your
  question.

  Should you ban pool values outside queries? Yes.

  It's the move that makes the whole model consistent, and it dissolves problems
  instead of patching them:

  - One way to touch pool data ‚ÄĒ through a query/map/system selector. That's the
  thing you can parallelize, GPU, reorder. pool.col[i] is an escape hatch that
  breaks all of that, and it's the hand-indexing you've objected to three times
  now.
  - It kills the singleton-[0] hack and the win global in one stroke ‚ÄĒ a [1]
  pool stops being "a global I index at [0]" and becomes a real queried pool.
  - Joins become the way to combine pools ‚ÄĒ which is the missing piece. render
  doesn't need a passed-in handle or Window.handle[0]; it queries Ball ‚čą Window
  ‚Üí each ball with the window. That's your "joined if a query over multiple
  archetypes."

  So the answer to "wtf is pos.x," the window, and gfx all collapse into the
  same rule: if you want a value from a pool, you query for it.

  gfx.clear querying for windows ‚ÄĒ agree, with one nuance

  gfx.clear queries the Window pool instead of taking a handle. The nuance:
  clearing calls into C (an effect), so it's a system over query{Window}, not a
  pure map ‚ÄĒ map is the branch-free pure kernel (E0046). It becomes a pure map
  only if the framebuffer itself becomes an arche pixel column (then clear is
  genuinely a columnar write). That's a bigger gfx redesign; the
  system-over-Window version gets you the query-driven shape now.

  - clear / present / poll ‚Üí system (query { Window }) ‚ÄĒ query the window, call
  the C op.
  - circle / render ‚Üí system (query { Ball, Window }) ‚ÄĒ each ball joined with
  the window, draw.

  The one thing the ban forces you to decide

  Test/debug observation. My columnar tests assert Acc.n[0] == 15 ‚ÄĒ that's also
  "a pool value outside a query." So either:
  - (a) make the ban a lint (error-by-default, --allow-pool-index) so
  tests/debug peeks opt out ‚ÄĒ matches your existing W-lint pattern; or
  - (b) verify only through query-systems (purer, but every test grows a checker
  system).

  I'd go (a) ‚ÄĒ a tunable lint. Ground-truth peeking in a test is legitimate;
  hand-indexing in program logic isn't.

  If you want it, the order (tests first, per your rule) is: write the lint's
  negative tests + rewrite the gfx/render shape to query-joins, then wire the
  lint. Want me to start ‚ÄĒ and is it lint (a) or hard-ban (b)?

‚óŹ Right ‚ÄĒ a join is a distinct relational operation, not a longer column list.
  The query language needs to express the relationship, and grow to not, or,
  etc. Let me frame it and get your call on syntax.

  The three cases you named, made precise:

  ‚ĒĆ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē¨‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē¨‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēź

  The hard part is cardinality: Ball & Window only has an obvious meaning when
  one side is a singleton ([1] ‚Üí broadcast: every ball sees the one window).
  General N√óM joins need a key or relationship (flecs (ChildOf, $parent)) ‚ÄĒ
  that's the same bucket as not/or: a relational algebra the query grows into.
  So I'd ship fan √ó singleton broadcast first (covers render), with the syntax
  designed to extend to the rest.

  I parked the lint test (left RED) ‚ÄĒ the query language is the real blocker and
  everything routes through its syntax. Pick the direction:

  ‚éŅ ¬†¬∑ How should a query express sources + relational ops (join/not/or), 
     distinct from a flat column list? (Sources in (), columns in {} / Operators
     inside the existing {} / Source variables (flecs-style))
     ¬∑ What join cardinality to support in the FIRST cut? (Singleton broadcast 
     only / Broadcast + keyed join)

‚ĚĮ the entire point of the query is to be source agnostic                        

‚óŹ Got it ‚ÄĒ that's the principle I violated. A query names components, never
  sources. query (Ball & Window) was exactly backwards: naming archetypes
  defeats the whole point. You ask for pos, color, handle and the engine finds
  whoever has them.

  So let me reframe joins to respect source-agnosticism:

  - Singleton broadcast is just component access. handle is a singleton
  component (one instance). query { pos, color, handle } ‚ÄĒ source-agnostic, you
  named three components; the engine resolves pos/color per matched entity and
  broadcasts the singleton handle. No "Ball", no "Window", no join keyword.
  That's render. The reason it matches 0 today is a bug: the matcher requires
  one archetype to hold all named components, instead of resolving each from
  wherever it lives.
  - Real entity‚ÜĒentity joins (the case that genuinely needs new expression) stay
  source-agnostic too: you don't name the other archetype, you name the
  relationship component that connects them (flecs (ChildOf, $p) style) plus a
  query variable. That's the same bucket as not/or ‚ÄĒ a relational algebra over
  components and relationships, never over sources.

  So the split is:

  ‚ĒĆ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē¨‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē¨‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēź

  ‚Ēā (future)        ‚Ēā components             ‚Ēā                             ‚Ēā
  ‚ĒĒ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēė

  The thing that makes render work is fixing the matcher to resolve each 
  component from its own pool (singleton ‚Üí broadcast), not adding source syntax.
  The dedicated join expression is only needed once you have entity‚ÜĒentity
  relationships.

  Is that the right read ‚ÄĒ singleton components need no special syntax (just
  name them, matcher resolves cross-pool), and explicit join syntax is reserved
  for relationship-based entity‚ÜĒentity joins?

‚úĽ Cogitated for 1m 14s

‚ĚĮ im thinking (query {foo}, query{bar}) or (Foo, Bar) where Foo and Bar are     
  querires                                                                      

‚óŹ That's clean ‚ÄĒ and it keeps every query source-agnostic. The join is a tuple 
  of queries, not a fatter query:

  Movers :: query { pos, color }
  Win    :: query { handle }

  draw :: system (Movers, Win) {            // join: fan over the product
    gfx.circle(handle, pos.x, pos.y, R, color)
  }
  // or inline:
  draw :: system (query { pos, color }, query { handle }) { ... }

  This nails the distinction you drew earlier ‚ÄĒ three genuinely different
  things, three different syntaxes:

  ‚ĒĆ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē¨‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē¨‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēź

  ‚Ēā 3 cols, one      ‚Ēā query { pos, vel, color }   ‚Ēā one entity has all     ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēā match            ‚Ēā                             ‚Ēā three                  ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§
  ‚Ēā join             ‚Ēā (query {pos}, query         ‚Ēā product of two queries ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēā                  ‚Ēā {handle})                   ‚Ēā                        ‚Ēā
  ‚Ēú‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēľ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ē§
  ‚Ēā 3 separate       ‚Ēā three separate systems      ‚Ēā independent            ‚Ēā
  ‚ĒĒ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēī‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚ĒÄ‚Ēė

  Each query in the tuple matches independently (source-agnostic), then they
  combine. The body sees the union of their columns; qualify on collision.

  The one real semantic question is cardinality of the product:
  - (Movers, Win) with Win a singleton (1 row) ‚Üí N√ó1 broadcast: every mover sees
  the one window. Unambiguous ‚ÄĒ this is render.
  - (Movers, Enemies) both N-row ‚Üí a true N√óM cross product, almost never what
  you want without a join key/relationship.

  So my proposal: the tuple-join requires all-but-one side to be a singleton
  (broadcast) to start. N√óM errors with "needs a relationship" until
  relationships exist ‚ÄĒ and that's where not/or/keyed-joins grow in, as
  operators on the queries in the tuple ((Movers, not Stunned), etc.). Same
  tuple, richer terms.

  That gives you render now and a clean home for the relational algebra later.
  Want me to spec it that way and start ‚ÄĒ tuple-of-queries selector,
  singleton-broadcast cardinality, matcher resolving each query from its own
  pool?

‚óŹ User approved Claude's plan
  ‚éŅ ¬†Plan saved to: ~/.claude/plans/alright-lets-implement-it-piped-pony.md ¬∑ 
     /plan to edit
     Source-agnostic joins + pool/global bans + rpg migration

     Context

     We converged (this session) on the data model now written in
     docs/design/queries-systems-and-joins.md:
     queries are source-agnostic (name components, never archetypes); bodies are
     columnar; a join is a
     tuple of queries (query{a}, query{b}); pools are the only mutable shared
     state. Two bans follow: no
     mutable globals (even private), and no Pool.col[i] outside a query.

     This is driven by a concrete, verified bug: the arche-rpg win: window
     mutable-opaque-global both violates
     the model and crashes (gfx.open(...)(win) ‚Üí spurious @drop ‚Üí stack
     overflow; earlier "renders" read
     stale PPMs). Putting the window in a [1]Window pool fixed it (verified:
     real PPM, 1839 px). But reading it
     back as Window.handle[0] is the hand-indexing we're banning ‚ÄĒ so the
     renderer needs joins to get the
     window without indexing. Joins + bans + the rpg migration are therefore one
     piece of work.

     Four RED tests already assert the target (written this session):
     tests/unit/language/systems/join_two_queries_{system,map}.arche,
     ‚Ä¶/pool_index_outside_query_rejected.arche,
     tests/unit/language/errors/private_mutable_global_rejected.arche. The
     columnar
     system_query_column_write.arche / archetype_query_interchangeable.arche are
     already GREEN.

     Decisions (from the user)

     - Scope = Everything: joins + both bans + migrate arche-rpg & gfx so the
     rpg renders proc-free,
     global-free, index-free.
     - Bans are tunable lints, enabled as ERRORS for the arche-rpg build and 
     every library it uses (gfx +
     stdlib core/fmt/os/io). Default level stays non-breaking for the wider
     arche suite (legitimate test peeks
     keep @allow / the suite default); the rpg/libs build turns them to hard
     error.
     - Joins are systems-only. map is a pure single-archetype GPU kernel ‚ÄĒ a
     tuple selector on map is an
     ERROR ("maps don't support joins"). So join_two_queries_map.arche flips to
     a rejection test.
     - Cardinality is an internal guardrail, not a user concept: a join
     broadcasts a [1] singleton across
     the N-row side; a genuine N√óM join errors ("needs a relationship/key"). No
     syntax for it.

     Part 1 ‚ÄĒ Tuple-of-queries join on system

     Extend the single-query selector to a comma-separated tuple. Each query
     resolves independently
     (source-agnostic); the body sees the union of columns.

     - Parser (parser/parser.c): system branch ~1531‚Äď1551. After the first
     query{}/Name is wrapped
     (1536/1542), loop on TOK_COMMA parsing more queries before the ) at¬†1548.
     Keep them as multiple
     SN_QUERY_EXPR/SN_QUERY_REF children of SN_SYSTEM_EXPR. map branch 
     ~1505‚Äď1519: if a comma is
     seen, error("maps don't support joins ‚ÄĒ use a system").
     - Semantic (semantic/semantic.c): bind_query_archetype (6232‚Äď6264) today
     matches ONE archetype to
     the whole param set. Generalize: resolve each query child to its own
     archetype (column-set match,
     reusing the 6235‚Äď6244 loop), tagging each ParamSummary with a query index.
     analyze_system_decl
     (6266‚Äď6287) binds all columns to scope. sem_resolve_map_queries (9708‚Äď9763)
     handles per-query named
     refs. Add the singleton-broadcast check: of the joined archetypes, all but
     one must be a [1] pool;
     else emit a "join needs a relationship/key" error.
     - HIR/lower (hir/hir.h, lower/lower.c): HirSystemDecl.params already a flat
     list ‚ÄĒ add a parallel
     int *param_query (or a query_index on HirParam). lower_query_columns
     (2251‚Äď2320) iterates each
     query node, flattening tuple-groups per query, recording the query index.
     - Codegen (codegen/codegen.c): codegen_system_decl query branch
     (10270‚Äď10381). Today: one pool, one
     row loop driven by its count (10305‚Äď10309), columns bound type-4 at
     implicit_loop_index (10323‚Äď10361,
     read at 3429‚Äď3451). For a join: pick the N-row pool as the driving loop;
     bind its columns at %row
     (as now); bind the singleton's columns as type-4 pointers read at constant 
     index 0 (broadcast).
     Add a query_index/broadcast flag to ValueInfo (15‚Äď30) so the column-read
     GEP (3434) uses %row for
     the driver and 0 for the broadcast side. query_match_archs (10960‚Äď10982) is
     called per query.

     Part 2 ‚ÄĒ Ban mutable globals, even private (extend W0022)

     sem_check_exported_mutable (semantic.c:8326‚Äď8343). The gate at line 8331
     (d->visibility != VIS_EXPORTED) is the only thing exempting #file/#module
     private globals. Drop the
     visibility condition so it fires on any mutable global; keep the existing
     exemptions (pools =
     STATIC_KIND_ARCHETYPE, :: consts = static_is_const) at 8333‚Äď8336. Broaden
     the W0022 message (drop
     "exported"). @allow(exported_mutable_global) and --exported-mutable keep
     working
     (cli/cli.c:15‚Äď26). Consider renaming slug ‚Üí mutable_global (new code or
     keep W0022 ‚ÄĒ keep W0022, just
     widen).

     Part 3 ‚ÄĒ New lint W0029 pool_index_outside_query

     Ban Pool.col[i] (explicit index whose base is an archetype/pool column)
     when NOT inside a query/map/system
     fan body. Plumbing follows W0022/W0024 exactly:
     - sem_diagnostics.h: SEM_LINT_pool_index_outside_query enum.
     - sem_diagnostics.c: table row { "W0029", "pool_index_outside_query", 
     CLASS_LINT, 1 }; g_werror[‚Ä¶]=1;

      10269   * body). Dispatched by the generated @arche_run (from the #
             run ScheduleTree). */
      10270 +/* The archetype that owns a column of this name (first in d
            +ecl order), or NULL. A query column resolves to             
      10271 + * its archetype by name ‚ÄĒ source-agnostic. Used to split a 
            +join's columns into the driver pool (looped) and            
      10272 + * `[1]` singleton pools (broadcast). */                    
      10273 +static const char *arch_owning_col(CodegenContext *ctx, cons
            +t char *col) {                                              
      10274 +  for (int d = 0; d < ctx->ast->decl_count; d++) {          
      10275 +    if (ctx->ast->decls[d]->kind != HIR_DECL_ARCHETYPE)     
      10276 +      continue;                                             
      10277 +    HirArchetypeDecl *arch = ctx->ast->decls[d]->data.archet
            +ype;                                                        
      10278 +    for (int f = 0; f < arch->field_count; f++)             
      10279 +      if (strcmp(arch->fields[f]->name, col) == 0)          
      10280 +        return arch->name;                                  
      10281 +  }                                                         
      10282 +  return NULL;                                              
      10283 +}                                                           
      10284 +                                                            
      10285 +/* Load a singleton column's value at index 0 (broadcast) as
            + a scalar SSA, binding it to `param_name`. */               
      10286 +static void bind_singleton_col(CodegenContext *ctx, const ch
            +ar *param_name, const char *arch_name) {                    
      10287 +  HirArchetypeDecl *arch = find_archetype_decl(ctx, arch_nam
            +e);                                                         
      10288 +  if (!arch)                                                
      10289 +    return;                                                 
      10290 +  int is_static = get_arch_static_capacity(ctx, arch_name) >
            + 0;                                                         
      10291 +  char base_buf[256];                                       
      10292 +  emit_query_pool_ptr(ctx, arch_name, is_static, base_buf, s
            +izeof(base_buf));                                           
      10293 +  for (int f = 0; f < arch->field_count; f++) {             
      10294 +    if (strcmp(arch->fields[f]->name, param_name) != 0)     
      10295 +      continue;                                             
      10296 +    const char *elem_type = llvm_type_from_arche(field_base_
            +type_name(arch->fields[f]->type));                          
      10297 +    char *elem_ptr;                                         
      10298 +    if (is_static) {                                        
      10299 +      elem_ptr = gen_value_name(ctx);                       
      10300 +      buffer_append_fmt(ctx, "  %s = getelementptr %%struct.
            +%s, %%struct.%s* %s, i32 0, i32 %d, i64 0\n",               
      10301 +                        elem_ptr, arch_name, arch_name, base
            +_buf, f);                                                   
      10302 +    } else {                                                
      10303 +      char *field_gep = gen_value_name(ctx);                
      10304 +      buffer_append_fmt(ctx, "  %s = getelementptr %%struct.
            +%s, %%struct.%s* %s, i32 0, i32 %d\n", field_gep,           
      10305 +                        arch_name, arch_name, base_buf, f); 
      10306 +      elem_ptr = gen_value_name(ctx);                       
      10307 +      buffer_append_fmt(ctx, "  %s = load %s*, %s** %s\n", e
            +lem_ptr, elem_type, elem_type, field_gep);                  
      10308 +    }                                                       
      10309 +    char *val = gen_value_name(ctx);                        
      10310 +    buffer_append_fmt(ctx, "  %s = load %s, %s* %s\n", val, 
            +elem_type, elem_type, elem_ptr);                            
      10311 +    add_value(ctx, param_name, val, 0);                     
      10312 +    break;                                                  
      10313 +  }                                                         
      10314 +}

‚ĚĮ also fx.circle takes in scalars how are you passing columns??                 

‚ĚĮ also you are rusing query handle everywhere you should just give it a name    

‚óŹ Three things to address. Let me take them in order.

  On scalars vs columns (gfx.circle takes ints, I'm passing pos.x): a system 
  over a query is a per-entity fan ‚ÄĒ the body runs once per matched entity, and
  inside it pos.x is bound to that entity's value (the engine walks the rows;
  codegen reads pos_x[row]). So gfx.circle receives a scalar each iteration, not
  a column. The query selects the columns; the fan hands you one entity's
  scalars at a time. (A map differs ‚ÄĒ it's whole-column data-parallel.)

  On reusing query { handle } ‚ÄĒ you're right. Archetypes and queries are
  interchangeable in the selector, so I'll just use the archetype name Window
  instead of repeating query { handle }. Same for the others ‚ÄĒ archetype names,
  no inline queries:

  Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

  So: a system is an effectful operation a device/module performs on its own 
  data/resource (the framebuffer), not a per-entity fan over a query. That's why
  raster = systems and render ‚Č† system.

‚úĽ Saut√©ed for 1m 53s

‚ĚĮ well really things like circle should be:                                     
                                                                                
  circle system (draws circle to window using the function)                     
  circle function (all the functional parts + composing the effects)            

‚óŹ That clicks ‚ÄĒ and it's the flat-effect model I'd been fumbling:

  - circle func = pure: the functional parts (the disc math ‚ÄĒ which pixels) + 
  composes the effect (builds the pixel-writes as an Eff value). No device
  touched.
  - circle system = runs that composed effect against the window's framebuffer ‚ÄĒ
  the actual draw.

  So func builds the effect, system runs it. That's the whole func (pure value,
  composes Eff) vs system (dispatches effects) split ‚ÄĒ and it's why raster
  belongs in systems (they run effects on the device) with the pure
  rasterization living in funcs. map stays the pure per-entity kernel; each the
  effectful per-entity iteration (deferred). I had system doing the per-entity
  fan, which is neither.

  Now I can see why everything I did was off: render/clear/etc. as system(query)
  conflated "run an effect" with "fan over entities."

  Before I rebuild raster this way, one real concern I want to flag rather than
  hit blindly: the shipped Eff layer is compile-time, single under-applied 
  extern (build(...)(out:) fused) ‚ÄĒ it composes one effect, not a loop of N
  pixel-writes. A disc is hundreds of writes computed in a loop. So "circle func
  composes the effect" likely needs the Eff layer to compose a variable number 
  of writes (the ¬ß6 column command-buffer that was deferred), which is a real
  extension, not just a refactor.

  So: is the move here to (a) build that ‚ÄĒ Eff composition over a loop of
  writes, so raster funcs can compose the framebuffer ops and systems run them ‚ÄĒ
  or (b) something smaller you have in mind for how circle func composes its
  writes? I don't want to guess the composition mechanism wrong again.

‚óŹ Traced it concretely. The raster loop after frame()() is used ‚ÄĒ in gfx.clear
  the final block stores the color through the px pointer (%v5) into the
  framebuffer:

  v44:
    %v52 = getelementptr i32, i32* %v5, i64 %v51   ; px[index]
    store i32 %arg1, i32* %v52                       ; px[index] = color

  %v5 is the framebuffer pointer that came back from frame, so the writes land
  in the backend buffer ‚ÄĒ that's literally what produces the rendered pixels.

  What is dead is inside frame itself:

  %v1 = load i32*, i32** %v0    ; reads the INCOMING px.ptr ‚ÄĒ never used
  %v3 = load i64,  i64*  %v2    ; reads the INCOMING px.len ‚ÄĒ never used

  frame's px is a write-only out-param, but codegen still loads its incoming
  value before overwriting it. Those two loads are genuinely unused.

  So ‚ÄĒ is that (the dead incoming-out-param reads) what you mean? Or are you
  pointing at the fact that frame is the only effect and everything after it is
  pure (the raster math), i.e. it shouldn't live in an effectful proc at all ‚ÄĒ
  it should be the func part? I want to be sure which "unused" you're seeing
  before I act.

‚úĽ Churned for 3m 12s

‚ĚĮ out is not write only. its read write                                         
                                                                                
  the problem is that everything after it is pure math but nothing is done with 
  any of that math (in theory, somehow something is still happening)            

‚óŹ Now I get it ‚ÄĒ and that's a sharp diagnosis.

  The raster loop mutates px, the slice frame handed back. In the value model
  that's pure local mutation: nothing reads or returns px afterward, so by the
  rules it should be dead ‚ÄĒ "nothing is done with the math." It only takes
  effect because px secretly aliases the device's framebuffer (it's
  gfx_be_frame's raw pointer sliced). So a write that looks like pure local work
  is actually a hidden, untracked device effect smuggled through a pointer 
  alias. The language thinks it's pure; the hardware disagrees. That's the rot.

  The func/Eff model fixes exactly this by making the framebuffer a value that 
  flows:

  - frame = an Eff ‚ÄĒ produces the framebuffer value (the one real "get" effect).
  - circle / clear = pure funcs ‚ÄĒ framebuffer-in ‚Üí framebuffer-out. The pixel
  math now produces a result that something is actually done with, instead of
  vanishing into an aliased local.
  - present = an Eff ‚ÄĒ consumes the framebuffer value and pushes it to the
  device.

  So the pipeline is fb = frame; fb = circle(fb, ‚Ä¶); fb = clear(fb, ‚Ä¶); 
  present(fb) ‚ÄĒ effects only at the get/put ends, pure transforms in the middle,
  and no hidden aliasing: the math's output is explicitly threaded and
  presented.

  Is that the model you're driving at ‚ÄĒ framebuffer-as-value, raster as pure
  func, frame/present as the only effects? If so I'll restructure raster/gfx
  that way (and that's what makes circle legitimately "a func + a system").

‚úĽ Saut√©ed for 39s

‚ÄĽ recap: Goal: make arche-rpg fully match the data model (proc-free, no hidden effects). Joins, both bans, and the rpg migration are done and rendering. Current task: restructure gfx/raster so the framebuffer flows as a value (frame/present as Effs, circle/clear as pure funcs). Next: confirm that model with you, then rewrite raster.arche.
‚ĚĮ how does a random out param binding alias an existing var?                    

‚óŹ You're right to call that out ‚ÄĒ it doesn't alias a variable. px is a fresh
  binding; nothing's aliased at the arche level. The aliasing is to foreign 
  memory, carried in the slice's pointer field:

  1. gfx_be_frame(win) is the extern ‚ÄĒ it returns a raw i32* straight into the
  C-side device buffer.
  2. frame wraps that raw pointer in a slice value: px = raw[0 : w*h] ‚Üí { ptr = 
  <device buffer>, len = w*h }.
  3. The out-param binding frame(win)(px:) just copies that slice struct (ptr +
  len) into the caller's fresh px.

  So px is a brand-new local ‚ÄĒ but its .ptr field holds a pointer into device
  memory. px[i] = color dereferences it and writes the device buffer. The
  "effect" rides inside the value (a raw foreign pointer in a slice), not
  through any variable aliasing. That's exactly why it looks pure (just a fresh
  slice you write into) while actually mutating device state ‚ÄĒ the extern handed
  arche a raw pointer and arche treats it as plain data.

  So my "aliases a var" was wrong; the precise statement is: frame launders a 
  raw device pointer into a slice value, and writes through that pointer are the
  hidden effect. Which is the real argument for framebuffer-as-value: don't
  hand out the raw device pointer at all ‚ÄĒ frame yields the framebuffer as an
  Eff-gated value, pure funcs transform it, present writes it back.

  parts + composing": math in, resulting framebuffer out.

  circle system ‚ÄĒ runs the effects. frame hands the framebuffer value in, the
  pure circle func transforms it, present writes it back. The threading is
  painted := circle(move fb, ‚Ä¶) ‚ÄĒ a fresh := binding, never fb = ‚Ä¶, so no slice
  gets repointed. Effects live only at the frame/present ends; the middle is
  pure.

  unresolved in my head ‚ÄĒ I suspect the system shouldn't iterate shapes at all,
  and an each over draw-commands applies the func.
  2. frame/present as Eff. I wrote frame(handle)(fb:, w:, h:) ‚ÄĒ the old
  out-param shape ‚ÄĒ but you said frame is an Eff. The Eff form is probably fb :=
  frame(handle) (a value), with present consuming a moved framebuffer. I don't
  know the surface syntax for an Eff-returning func yet.
  3. The framebuffer's type. []int is a slice ‚ÄĒ the very thing with the repoint
  hazard, and runtime-sized. A real "framebuffer value" wants to be an owned 
  buffer, but arche arrays are fixed-size. So own []int + move is my
  approximation, not something I'm sure is right.
  4. Two decls named circle (func + system) ‚ÄĒ an overload by form; not sure the
  language allows it or if the system should just be draw.

  Did I get the core split right (func = pure framebuffer transform, system =
  run frame/present around it), and is my instinct correct that iterating the
  shapes is each, not the system?

‚úĽ Brewed for 3m 12s

‚ĚĮ explain what frame and present are doing                                      

‚óŹ frame and present are the two device-boundary effects that bracket a frame's
  drawing ‚ÄĒ get the canvas, then show it:

  frame ‚ÄĒ acquire the drawing surface (the GET effect). It asks the backend for
  the current framebuffer: gfx_be_frame(win) returns the pixel buffer,
  gfx_be_w/h its current size. Conceptually: "hand me the canvas to paint on, at
  its current dimensions." It's re-acquired every iteration precisely because
  the window can resize ‚ÄĒ the surface and its dims can change frame to frame.

  present ‚ÄĒ commit the painted surface (the PUT effect). gfx_be_present(win)
  flushes that buffer to the actual display (X11: blit into the window;
  headless: write the PPM). Conceptually: "show what I painted."

  So a frame is frame ‚Üí (pure paint) ‚Üí present: acquire the canvas, paint it
  with pure funcs, show it. Effects only at the two ends.

  The honest tension this exposes ‚ÄĒ and I think it's the real point you're
  driving at: today frame and present operate on the same device-owned buffer.
  frame hands back a raw pointer into device memory, you paint in place, present
  just flushes it. One buffer, zero copies ‚ÄĒ but that's exactly why "pure
  paint" is secretly mutating device memory (the laundered pointer).

  In the value model they have to decouple: frame yields the framebuffer as a
  value you own, the pure func produces a new framebuffer, and present writes 
  that value back to the device. That removes the hidden aliasing ‚ÄĒ but it
  forces a real question: who allocates the framebuffer, and does present copy
  it to the device (one explicit blit at the boundary) or does arche own the
  pixels outright? That ownership decision is the thing that makes frame/present
  honest effects instead of a shared-pointer side channel ‚ÄĒ and it's where I'd
  want your call before building it.

‚óŹ That reads as one expression = one fused action:

  frame(handle) |> circle(cx, cy, r, color) |> present(handle)

  - frame(handle) ‚Üí Eff(Frame) ‚ÄĒ acquire the framebuffer as a value (Frame =
  {px, w, h}), no raw pointer escaping.
  - |> circle(cx,cy,r,color) ‚Üí fmap the pure circle func (Frame ‚Üí Frame) over
  the Eff ‚ÄĒ paints, touches no device.
  - |> present(handle) ‚Üí the put, consuming the painted Frame.

  So the whole draw is a single composed Eff, built from one pure func bracketed
  by the two boundary effects. Because the Eff layer is compile-time/fused,
  frame ‚Üí paint ‚Üí present collapse into one routine ‚ÄĒ that's "the entire thing
  as one proc," except it's synthesized from a pure func + effect endpoints
  instead of a hand-written effectful blob. And (Window, Circle) supplies both
  ends: handle from Window, cx/cy/r/color from Circle (the draw command). The
  Frame flows through |> as a value, never repointed.

  Two things I'm genuinely unsure of ‚ÄĒ tell me which way:

  1. |> is doing two different jobs here. circle is pure (Frame ‚Üí Frame) so that
  |> is fmap; but present is an effect (Frame ‚Üí Eff), so that last |> is really
  bind/run, not fmap. Is |> meant to be the generalized pipe that's fmap when
  the RHS is pure and bind when it's effectful ‚ÄĒ or should the terminal present
  use a different operator?
  2. N circles. With (Window, Circle) and many circles, does this fan per-circle
  (frame+present each time ‚ÄĒ clearly wrong) or do the N circle-paints fold over
  one framebuffer between a single frame and single present? I believe you want
  the latter ‚ÄĒ |> chaining all the paints into one acquire/present ‚ÄĒ but then
  the system isn't really iterating; the join is feeding a fold. That's the
  piece where I'm least sure the shape is right.

‚úĽ Worked for 2m 22s

‚ĚĮ what is "Frame"                                                               

‚óŹ Honestly? Frame is a placeholder I invented, and I don't think it's justified
  ‚ÄĒ which is probably why you're asking.

  I reached for it because the |> pipeline needs one value to thread (frame ‚Üí 
  circle ‚Üí present), so I bundled { px, w, h } into a struct and called it
  Frame. But the framebuffer isn't some free-floating struct ‚ÄĒ it's the Window's
  own data. The pixels and dimensions belong to the window. So there shouldn't
  be a separate Frame type at all; frame(handle) should hand back the Window's
  framebuffer (its pixels + size), and present(handle) pushes those same pixels.

  So the honest correction: Frame should just be the Window's framebuffer ‚ÄĒ i.e.
  the Window archetype carries the pixels (a px column) and w/h, and
  frame/present are the effects that read/commit that. The thing flowing through
  |> is the window's pixel buffer, not a new type.

  Which then exposes the question I keep circling: where do the pixels actually 
  live? Device-owned C memory (then frame is unavoidably handing you a pointer
  into it ‚ÄĒ the laundering), or an arche-owned px buffer on the Window pool
  (then present is the explicit blit to the device). The Frame-vs-no-Frame
  question is really that storage/ownership question wearing a costume ‚ÄĒ and
  that's the call I need from you, not a type I should be inventing.

  2. Two functions, not one: a pure paint func (the current disc math) and a
  circle func that composes frame |> paint |> present into one Eff.

‚óŹ The shape now:

  - paint ‚ÄĒ pure. Operates on the Window pool's px (write-through, legal;
  returns it). Just disc math, no device.
  - circle ‚ÄĒ composes frame |> paint |> present into one Eff. Pure func that
  builds the action.
  - circle system (Window, Circle) ‚ÄĒ dispatches it: handle/w/h from the Window
  pool (opaque handle + px + dims), cx/cy/r/color from Circle.

  The Eff fusion is what makes this honest: frame |> paint |> present looks like
  pure value flow, but the compile-time Eff layer collapses it to in-place
  writes on the pool's px ‚ÄĒ no copy, and crucially no raw pointer, since the
  only C thing is the opaque handle that present blits through.

  Two things I still don't think I have right ‚ÄĒ and they're the real ones:

  1. Is frame even an effect now? If px lives in the Window pool (arche-owned),
  then frame isn't doing FFI ‚ÄĒ it's just handing you the pool's px. The only
  device effect would be present (blit px ‚Üí screen via the opaque handle). So
  maybe the pipeline is really paint(px) |> present(handle) with px coming
  straight from the Window query, and frame only exists if the pixels are
  device-owned (which your "storage in pools" rule says they shouldn't be). I
  suspect frame should disappear.
  2. N circles. system (Window, Circle) dispatching circle() once per circle
  re-acquires/re-presents per shape ‚ÄĒ wrong. You want all the paints to fold 
  over one px between a single acquire and a single present. So the system can't
  be paint-then-present per circle; the |> present has to sit outside the
  per-circle fold. I don't yet see how (Window, Circle) + |> expresses "fold
  paints, present once" rather than "present each."

‚ĚĮ you run an eff with () the out params, not with "run" infact I think run is   
  going away completely soon now that we have #run run is pointless I think     

‚óŹ Right ‚ÄĒ an Eff is run by applying its out-params with () (build(args)(out:)),
  not run. So the composer circle(handle, ‚Ä¶) builds the Eff and the trailing ()
  runs it:

‚óŹ Update(extras/gfx/raster.arche)
  ‚éŅ ¬†Added 1 line, removed 1 line
      71  }
      72  
      73  circle :: system (Window, Circle) {
      74 -  run circle(handle, w, h, cx, cy, r, color);                  
      74 +  circle(handle, w, h, cx, cy, r, color)();                    
      75  }

‚óŹ That tracks ‚ÄĒ and it closes the loop on the whole thread:

  - #run = the orchestrator (the schedule). The only place dispatch is composed.
  - Eff = run by applying out-params with ().
  - So run X (the statement) is redundant ‚ÄĒ it was the thing letting a system
  imperatively dispatch another (the "super-system" smell, like pace running
  step). Kill it and that anti-pattern can't even be written: you either
  schedule via #run, or run an Eff via (). Nothing in a body reaches over and
  runs a system/map.

  It also retroactively flags what I did earlier: sim :: system { run step; }
  and pace ‚Ä¶ run game.step were both using the doomed run. Once it's gone, step
  (a map) is scheduled by #run directly (the deferred map-in-scheduler), not
  invoked from inside a system body.

  So the corrected circle system body is just circle(handle, w, h, cx, cy, r, 
  color)() ‚ÄĒ build the Eff, run it with (). raster.arche stays the non-building
  sketch.

  Want me to capture this whole model (func builds Eff / system runs effects /
  map¬∑each = the fans / queries give columns / joins = tuple / slices can't
  repoint / run retiring / storage in pools, opaque-only FFI) into docs/design/
  so it stops drifting between turns? I think that's overdue.

‚úĽ Cooked for 55s

‚ĚĮ also a system hands you columns                                               

‚óŹ That's the missing piece ‚ÄĒ and it resolves both my open questions.

  A system hands you the columns of its query/join ‚ÄĒ not per-entity scalars, not
  a fan. So in circle :: system (Window, Circle), handle/w/h/px are the Window
  columns and cx/cy/r/color are the Circle columns ‚ÄĒ whole columns. The system
  is just the effectful context that's been handed the data and composes effects
  over it.

  That kills the N-circles confusion: circle(handle, w, h, cx, cy, r, color)()
  isn't run once per circle ‚ÄĒ it's handed the column of circles, so the composed
  Eff does frame once, paint across all of them (the columnar/pure work),
  present once. The fold-over-shapes is just columnar data, not iteration.

  And it finally pins down what a system is, distinct from the rest:
  - map ‚ÄĒ handed columns, pure per-element transform.
  - each ‚ÄĒ handed columns, effectful per-element iteration.
  - system ‚ÄĒ handed columns, composes/runs effects over them (via funcs building
  Eff, run with ()). Not per-element at all.
  - #run ‚ÄĒ orchestrates systems.

  So my original system(query) was wrong on two counts: it handed per-row
  scalars instead of columns, and it ran a per-entity body instead of composing
  an Eff. Both are now clear.

  This model is basically complete and I keep nearly-losing it between turns ‚ÄĒ
  let me write it into docs/design/ now (what each of map/each/system/func/#run
  is, columns-not-scalars, Eff via (), run retiring, slices can't repoint,
  storage-in-pools + opaque-only FFI, joins = tuple of queries). Want that?

  already pool-owned, not fetched from the device):

  circle :: system (Window, Circle) {
    circle(handle, px, w, h, cx, cy, r, color)();
  }

  - circle(‚Ä¶) builds the Eff, () runs it.
  - The composer is now paint(px, ‚Ä¶) |> present(handle) ‚ÄĒ no frame (the pixels

  effect, blitting px out through the opaque handle.

  One thing still fuzzy for me: cx/cy/r/color arrive as columns (all the
  circles), so paint is really folding every disc into the one px ‚ÄĒ i.e. paint
  over a column of circles is a per-shape operation. That smells like paint
  should be a map (pure, per-circle, writing into the shared px) rather than a
  plain func taking scalars. Is the paint step a map and circle the system that
  wraps it in present?
‚úĽ Cooked for 1m 41s

‚ĚĮ how does this work because I thought that free applicatives couldn't depend   
  on outputs from earlier effects                                               
                                                                                
    return frame(handle) |> paint(w, h, cx, cy, r, color) |> present(handle);   

‚óŹ You're exactly right, and that's the crux ‚ÄĒ frame |> paint |> present can't be
  a free applicative, and that's precisely why I had to delete frame.

  Walk the types:
  - frame(handle) |> paint(‚Ä¶) ‚ÄĒ paint is pure (px ‚Üí px), so that |> is fmap.
  Fine for a functor/applicative.
  - ‚Ä¶ |> present(handle) ‚ÄĒ present is an effect, and its input is the
  framebuffer that frame produced at runtime. So this |> is bind, not fmap: a
  later effect depending on an earlier effect's output. That's monadic. A free
  applicative can't express it ‚ÄĒ you nailed it.

  The fix is your storage-in-pools rule, which is what removing frame did:

  - With frame, the framebuffer is an effect output ‚Üí present depends on it ‚Üí
  monadic ‚Üí impossible in the applicative.
  - With px living in the Window pool (handed to the system as a column), the
  framebuffer is shared state, not an effect result. paint is a pure transform
  of that pool data, and present is the only effect ‚ÄĒ it consumes a pure value,
  depending on no other effect's output.

  So the current pipeline paint(px, ‚Ä¶) |> present(handle) is applicative-clean
  by construction: there's exactly one effect, and nothing's runtime input comes
  from another effect. The dependency you'd need a monad for got absorbed into
  the pool ‚ÄĒ the buffer is read/written as ordinary pool state, so the effects
  stay independent.

  That's actually the deep reason "long-lived storage in pools" isn't just a
  style rule: it's what keeps the effect layer applicative instead of forcing a
  free monad. frame-as-an-effect was smuggling a monadic dependency in; killing
  it is mandatory, not optional.

       51  
       54 -This keeps every query source-agnostic and distinguishes the t
          -hree genuinely different things:

       60 +  the framebuffer that a `present` effect commits ‚ÄĒ that is ex
          +actly the forbidden monadic dependency.

          +the system as columns), and the effects stop                  
       62 +  threading outputs to each other. The pure transforms in betw

       63 +  effects are the **boundary commits**. Independent effects ‚Üí

       94 -

       96 -it flows by `move`/borrow/return and is **never overwritten**

          -e a pool slot's lifecycle (create/destroy) is

          - opaque slot**: assigning over an opaque

          -ata** (a `[1]Window` pool), not a mutable                     
      100 -opaque global ‚ÄĒ the global form both violates rule 1 and crash
          -es (spurious `@drop`). See

‚óŹ Update(docs/design/queries-systems-and-joins.md)
  ‚éŅ ¬†Added 18 lines
      65  **FFI**: avoid it; when a C pointer is unavoidable it must be *
          *opaque** (never a raw pointer handed to
      66  arche ‚ÄĒ see slices).
      67  
      68 +## A procedure is composed, not a kind                         
      69 +                                                               
      70 +There is no `proc` ‚ÄĒ and more deeply, **a "procedure" (a multi-
         +step effectful action) is not a declared kind                  
      71 +at all.** It is *composed*: pure `func`s build `Eff` values, `|
         +>` threads a pure transform through an effect,                 
      72 +and a `system` runs the result with `()`. The effectfulness liv
         +es in the **composition**, never in a keyword.                 
      73 +                                                               
      74 +So "make the whole draw one procedure" means *compose* it ‚ÄĒ    
      75 +                                                               
      76 +```                                                            
      77 +circle(handle, px, w, h, cx, cy, r, color)()                   
      78 +```                                                            
      79 +                                                               
      80 +‚ÄĒ a single action synthesized from the pure `paint` func and th
         +e `present` boundary effect, not a monolithic                  
      81 +`proc { ‚Ä¶ }` block. What used to be one opaque effectful kind i
         +s now three separable things: **pure**                         
      82 +(`func`) + **effect at the boundary** (the `Eff`) + **orchestra
         +tion** (`system` / `#run`). Nothing *names*                    
      83 +"the procedure" ‚ÄĒ it is the shape you get by composing those th
         +ree, and that is the whole reason `proc` is                    
      84 +gone.                                                          
      85 +                                                               
      86  ## Slices
      87  
      88  A slice is a **view**: `{ ptr, len }`. **Its pointer is fixed a
          t creation.** You may write *through* it

‚óŹ Doc folded ‚ÄĒ the full model plus the applicative/pools insight and the
  "procedure is composed, not a kind" section are now in
  docs/design/queries-systems-and-joins.md. Entering plan mode to plan the
  implementation:

‚ĚĮ so explain why you are still treating system as an each?                      

‚óŹ Because of the func signature ‚ÄĒ that's the tell, and you're right.

  circle/paint take scalar cx, cy, r, color ‚ÄĒ one circle. But the system is
  handed the Circle column ‚ÄĒ N circles ‚ÄĒ and I pass that column straight into
  the scalar call circle(handle, px, ‚Ä¶, cx, cy, r, color)(). A scalar function
  applied to a column only means anything if it's invoked once per element. So
  even though I keep saying "the system is handed columns," I immediately funnel
  those columns into a per-circle scalar call ‚ÄĒ which can only work by
  iterating the column. That iteration is an each. I moved the fan out of the
  body's syntax but smuggled it right back in through the scalar signature.

  A system never iterates. It's handed whole columns and composes/runs effects
  over them. The per-circle work ‚ÄĒ one disc per circle ‚ÄĒ has to live in an
  explicit per-element construct:

  - if it were branch-free/pure it'd be a map over Circle,
  - but the disc has clamps + a radius test (control flow), so it's actually an
  each over Circle (effectful per-element, writing each disc into the Window's
  px).

  So the corrected shape is: an each (Circle) does the per-disc drawing into px,
  and the system just composes that with the single present ‚ÄĒ it hands Circle
  to the each and Window to present; it does not loop anything itself. My scalar
  circle func is the bug: the moment a system feeds a column into a per-element
  scalar, the system has become an each.

  Which is also why you said each would be needed here ‚ÄĒ the per-shape draw
  genuinely is one. Want me to redo circle with the fan as an explicit each 
  (Circle) and the system purely composing each-into-px then present?

‚úĽ Brewed for 1m 9s

‚ĚĮ why and how is px |>                                                          

‚óŹ It doesn't, and that's the mistake. |> is fmap over an Eff ‚ÄĒ Eff(T) |> (T ‚Üí U)
  = Eff(U). Its left operand has to be an Eff; its right is a pure func. px is
  plain pool data ([]int), not an Eff ‚ÄĒ so px |> ‚Ä¶ is ill-typed. There's no
  effect there to map over.

  I wrote px |> because I was using |> as a generic value-pipe (F#/Elixir style:
  "thread this value through these functions"). arche's |> isn't that ‚ÄĒ it's
  specifically Eff-fmap. So:

  - px |> paint(‚Ä¶) should just be paint(px, ‚Ä¶) ‚ÄĒ a plain pure call. No |>.
  - ‚Ä¶ |> present(‚Ä¶) ‚ÄĒ present is the effect that consumes the result, which is
  running/consuming, not fmap.

  And the deeper consequence: once frame is gone (px lives in the pool), there 
  is no Eff on the draw path for a |> to start from. The old frame(handle) |>
  worked because frame was an extern that produced a value-bearing Eff you could
  fmap pure funcs over. Drawing has none of that ‚ÄĒ paint is a pure transform of
  plain data, and present is a terminal void effect. So there's nothing to |>.

  A |> would only show up where an extern yields a value-bearing Eff that pure
  funcs then transform ‚ÄĒ e.g. poll() returning is_open. The draw is just: pure
  paint(px, ‚Ä¶) producing the pixels, handed to the one effect present. No pipe.

  So px |> paint |> present was wrong twice: px isn't an Eff, and present isn't
  a pure func ‚ÄĒ neither end is what |> takes. The honest version is present (the
  effect) applied to paint(px, ‚Ä¶) (pure) ‚ÄĒ built as an Eff, run with (), and no
  |> at all.

‚óŹ Done. The desired shape, and why each piece is what it is:

  circle :: each (Circle, Window) ‚ÄĒ the per-circle draw, with the iteration
  explicit. It's handed the Circle column (cx/cy/r/color, per element) joined
  with the Window [1] singleton (px/w/h, broadcast to every circle), and writes
  each disc into the window's px. It's an each, not a map, because the disc has
  control flow (the clamps + radius test) ‚ÄĒ map is branch-free. This is where
  the fan honestly lives; it is no longer smuggled into a system through a
  scalar signature.

  present :: system (Window) ‚ÄĒ handed the Window column, it just runs the one 
  boundary effect: blit(handle, px) builds the Eff (copy px to the device
  through the opaque handle), () runs it. The system composes/runs effects and
  never iterates.

  What's gone, and why:
  - No |>, no composer func, no paint ‚ÄĒ there's no value-bearing Eff on the draw
  path to fmap over (frame was that, and it's gone). The painting is just
  columnar writes to the px pool column (legal pool-data writes); the only
  device effect is the blit.
  - No px |> ‚ÄĒ px is data, not an Eff.
  - The two are ordered by #run: circle (each ‚Üí fills px), then present (system
  ‚Üí blits). The framebuffer lives in the Window pool the whole time; the each
  writes it, the system commits it.

  So the split is finally clean: each fans, system runs the effect, #run orders 
  them, and the pool holds the pixels ‚ÄĒ which is exactly what keeps it
  applicative (the each's writes and the blit don't thread outputs through each
  other; they share pool state).

‚úĽ Crunched for 2m 29s

‚ĚĮ this seems to be a step backwards. is it really better to use each instead of 
  using system and owning the loop? or is it the same?                          
                                                                                
  also where is the func/proc? because people will want the ability to run a    
  single draw cirlce "proc" (eff + out params)                                  

‚óŹ Good questions ‚ÄĒ these are the real design ones.

  each vs a system owning the loop ‚ÄĒ not the same, and each is better (not a 
  step back):

  A system can't cleanly own that loop. To iterate the circles by hand it would
  have to write Circle.cx[i] ‚ÄĒ hand-indexing a pool column, which is exactly the
  W0029 ban. And a hand loop is opaque to the compiler: it can't be reordered,
  parallelized, or (if pure) lowered to a GPU map. each is the declarative
  version of the same loop: the engine owns the iteration, binds the columns per
  element (no indexing), and keeps the optimization headroom. Same result, but
  each is the loop without the hand-index and with the parallelism ‚ÄĒ so it's
  strictly forward, not sideways.

  Where the func/proc went ‚ÄĒ you're right, it's needed. I over-rotated and
  deleted the one-off path. There should be both: a func that builds a 
  single-circle draw Eff (the "proc" ‚ÄĒ run with () + out-params for someone
  drawing one circle), and the each that batches the column. They share the pure
  paint:

‚óŹ Update(extras/gfx/raster.arche)
  ‚éŅ ¬†Added 10 lines, removed 1 line

      47  }

         +r: int, color: int) -> []int {

      52    if (yy < 0) {
     ...

      71 +}

‚óŹ Now there are four pieces, each with one job:

  - paint (func, pure) ‚ÄĒ the shared unit: the disc math, px ‚Üí px. No effect.
  - circle (func ‚Üí Eff) ‚ÄĒ the one-off "proc" you asked about: blit(handle, 
  paint(px, ‚Ä¶)) builds the draw-one-circle action (paint the disc, then commit).
  Someone drawing a single circle calls circle(handle, px, ‚Ä¶)() ‚ÄĒ Eff + run
  with ().
  - draw (each) ‚ÄĒ the batch: paint every Circle into the shared px, no commit
  per shape.
  - present (system) ‚ÄĒ commit once: blit(handle, px)().

  The split that matters: the one-off func bundles paint + blit (draw and show
  one circle); the batch factors blit out (draw paints all, present blits once)
  so you don't commit N times for N circles. Both reuse paint, so there's no
  duplicated disc math.

  So your two concerns resolve into: each is the loop done right (engine-owned,
  no hand-index, parallelizable), and the single-draw "proc" is alive and well
  as the circle func ‚ÄĒ each is literally just that unit's pure core (paint)
  applied across a column, with the commit lifted out. The func is for "draw me
  one circle," the each+system is for "draw this whole column of circles."

  Still a sketch (each, blit, Eff-of-a-void-effect, the dup circle/paint
  overloads aren't built) ‚ÄĒ but the role of every line is now what we want.

‚óŹ Now everything uses the return:

  - circle (func, pure) ‚ÄĒ paint one disc, return the framebuffer. The unit.
  - draw (each) ‚ÄĒ the fold: px = circle(px, ‚Ä¶) per circle, threading the running
  framebuffer. Each step consumes the previous return.
  - present (system) ‚ÄĒ blit(handle, px)() once.
  - one-off ‚ÄĒ blit(handle, circle(px, ‚Ä¶))(): circle (pure) makes the painted px,
  blit (Eff) commits it, run with (). Uses the return.

  One honest consequence this surfaces: because each circle threads px from the
  last one, draw is sequential ‚ÄĒ a fold/scan over the Circle column, not an
  independent parallel each. That's a real distinction (an independent each/map
  could run in any order / on the GPU; a px-accumulating fold can't). So this is
  closer to a scan over the circles than a plain each ‚ÄĒ which fits, since they
  all write the one shared framebuffer and order matters on overlap.

  So the dead-call is gone, and it exposed that the batch is genuinely an
  accumulator fold, not a parallel fan.

‚úĽ Baked for 2m 38s

‚ĚĮ so is px part of circle... or...?                                             

‚óŹ px is part of Window, not Circle.

  A Circle is just the shape ‚ÄĒ cx, cy, r, color. The framebuffer px (plus w, h)
  belongs to the Window ‚ÄĒ one canvas per window. So in each (Circle, Window):

  - cx/cy/r/color come from the Circle column (per element ‚ÄĒ the shapes),
  - px/w/h come from the Window [1] singleton (broadcast ‚ÄĒ the one shared
  canvas).

  The circle func isn't "a circle" ‚ÄĒ it's "paint a circle onto a framebuffer,"
  so it takes both: the canvas (px, from Window) and the shape (cx‚Ä¶, from
  Circle), and returns the canvas. The fold px = circle(px, ‚Ä¶) threads the
  Window's px through every Circle.

  So if anything my naming oversells it ‚ÄĒ the func is really
  paint_circle(canvas, shape) -> canvas. px is Window state being accumulated
  into; the Circle column just supplies the shapes that get folded onto it. Is
  that the split you're checking ‚ÄĒ that the canvas is Window's and the shape is
  Circle's, and the func bridges them?

‚úĽ Cooked for 35s

‚ĚĮ the move kills px so you have to thread it px :=                              

‚óŹ Right ‚ÄĒ circle takes own px, so the call moves px in, which consumes (kills)
  the old binding. You can't = back onto a dead binding; you rebind a fresh one
  with :=, and move at the call site:

‚óŹ Update(extras/gfx/raster.arche)
  ‚éŅ ¬†Added 1 line, removed 1 line
      67  }
      68  
      69  draw :: each (Circle, Window) {
      70 -  px = circle(px, w, h, cx, cy, r, color);                     
      70 +  px := circle(move px, w, h, cx, cy, r, color);               
      71  }
      72  
      73  present :: system (Window) {

‚óŹ Got it. The mechanics: circle(own px) means the call consumes px via move ‚ÄĒ
  after move px, the old px binding is dead, so px := rebinds the framebuffer
  that circle hands back. Linear threading: moved in, rebound out, each step.
  Zero-copy (the storage is the same, ownership just travels), and it fuses to
  in-place ‚ÄĒ but at the surface it's a clean affine flow with no aliasing and
  nothing repointed.

  Same for the one-off:

  painted := circle(move px, w, h, cx, cy, r, color);
  blit(handle, move painted)()

  move px in, rebind painted, move it into blit. The framebuffer is never copied
  and never aliased ‚ÄĒ it's owned and handed along.

  So the full chain is honest now: the Window owns px; each moves it through the
  circle fold (px := circle(move px, ‚Ä¶)); present blits the final one. No dead
  calls, no repoints, no laundered pointers ‚ÄĒ the move/rebind is what threads
  the canvas linearly through the shapes.

‚óŹ Update(docs/design/queries-systems-and-joins.md)
  ‚éŅ ¬†Added 11 lines, removed 7 lines
       9  Everything below that touches pool data is **handed columns** b
          y its query ‚ÄĒ not per-entity scalars, not a
      10  hidden row cursor. What differs is what each one is *allowed to
           do* with those columns:
      11  
      12 -- **`func`** ‚ÄĒ a pure value. Reads no pool/global state. Its jo
         -b is to **compute** and to **build `Eff`                       
      13 -  values** (compose effects as data). Never runs an effect.    
      12 +- **`func`** ‚ÄĒ a pure value. Reads no pool/global state. **Comp
         +utes** (returns values) and **builds `Eff`                     
      13 +  values**. Never runs an effect. Its **return must be consumed
         +** ‚ÄĒ calling a func and discarding the result                  
      14 +  is a no-op the compiler deletes (there were no side effects t
         +o keep). To thread state you rebind the                        
      15 +  return: `px := paint(move px, ‚Ä¶)`.                           
      16  - **`map`** ‚ÄĒ handed columns; a **pure** per-element kernel. Br
          anch-free, effect-free (E0046), GPU-portable.
      15 -- **`each`** ‚ÄĒ handed columns; an **effectful** per-element ite
         -ration (for genuine per-element effects). *(Not                
      16 -  yet built.)*                                                 
      17 -- **`system`** ‚ÄĒ handed columns; **composes and runs effects** 
         -over them (calls funcs that build `Eff`s, runs                 
      18 -  them). A system is **not** a per-element fan ‚ÄĒ it is the effe
         -ctful context that has the columns and drives                  
      19 -  the boundary effects.                                        
      17 +- **`each`** ‚ÄĒ handed columns; the **per-element fan** when the
         + work has control flow / effects (a `map` that                 
      18 +  isn't branch-free). If each element is **independent**, it pa
         +rallelizes like a `map`. If it threads an                      
      19 +  **accumulator** (each step consumes the previous result ‚ÄĒ fol
         +ding shapes onto one framebuffer), it is a                     
      20 +  **sequential fold/scan**, not parallel. *(Not yet built.)*   
      21 +- **`system`** ‚ÄĒ handed columns; **runs effects** over them (bu
         +ilds `Eff`s via funcs, runs them with `()`). A                 
      22 +  system **never iterates**: the instant it feeds a column into
         + a per-element scalar call it has secretly                     
      23 +  become an `each`. It only composes/runs the **boundary effect
         +s**.                                                           
      24  - **`#run`** ‚ÄĒ the orchestrator: the compile-time-folded schedu
          le. The only place dispatch is composed.
      25  
      26  Removed / retiring: **`proc`** (gone ‚ÄĒ split into `func` that b
          uilds and `system`/effects that run);

       99  
      100 -The framebuffer **pixels live in the `Window` pool** (`px` col
          -umn) alongside the **opaque** handle and dims.                
      101 -Drawing splits into a pure func and a system that runs the one
          - boundary effect:                                             
      100 +The **canvas lives in the `Window` pool** (`px` + dims + the *
          +*opaque** handle). A `Circle` is just a                       
      101 +**shape** (`cx, cy, r, color`) ‚ÄĒ it does not own pixels. Three
          + pieces: a pure unit, a fold that batches it,                 
      102 +and the one boundary effect.                                  
      103  
      104  ```
      104 -paint :: func(own px: []int, w: int, h: int, cx: int, cy: int,
          - r: int, color: int) -> []int { ‚Ä¶ }   // pure                 
      105 +// canvas is Window state; a Circle is just a shape           
      106 +Window :: arche { handle :: window  px :: []int  w :: int  h :
          +: int }                                                       
      107 +Circle :: arche { cx :: int  cy :: int  r :: int  color :: int
          + }                                                            
      108  
      106 -circle :: func(handle: window, own px: []int, w: int, h: int, 
          -cx: int, cy: int, r: int, color: int) -> Eff {                
      107 -  return paint(px, w, h, cx, cy, r, color) |> present(handle);
          -   // build the Eff                                           
      109 +// pure UNIT: paint one disc onto a framebuffer, and RETURN th
          +e framebuffer (the return is the whole point)                 
      110 +circle :: func(own px: []int, w: int, h: int, cx: int, cy: int
          +, r: int, color: int) -> []int { ‚Ä¶ return px }                
      111 +                                                              
      112 +// BATCH: a sequential fold over the shapes ‚ÄĒ move the canvas 
          +through each circle and rebind the result                     
      113 +circles :: each (Circle, Window) {                            
      114 +  px := circle(move px, w, h, cx, cy, r, color);              
      115  }
      116  
      110 -circle :: system (Window, Circle) {           // handed the Wi
          -ndow + Circle COLUMNS                                         
      111 -  circle(handle, px, w, h, cx, cy, r, color)();   // build + r
          -un with ()                                                    
      117 +// COMMIT once: the only device effect (blit px to the device 
          +via the opaque handle), run with ()                           
      118 +present :: system (Window) {                                  
      119 +  blit(handle, px)();                                         
      120  }
      121  ```
      122  
      115 -- `paint` is pure (transforms the pool's `px`). `present` is t
          -he **only** effect ‚ÄĒ it blits `px` to the                     
      116 -  device through the **opaque** handle. There is **no `frame` 
          -effect**: the pixels are pool state, not an                   
      117 -  effect output, so the pipeline stays applicative.           
      118 -- `circle` the system is handed *columns* (`px`, `handle`, `cx
          -`‚Ä¶). It composes the `Eff` and runs it with                   
      119 -  `()`; it does not iterate per shape itself ‚ÄĒ the columns are
          - the shapes.                                                  
      123 +- **`px` is Window state, not Circle's.** `circle` is really `
          +paint_circle(canvas, shape) -> canvas`: it                    
      124 +  takes the canvas (from `Window`, broadcast `[1]`) and a shap
          +e (from the `Circle` column) and hands the                    
      125 +  canvas back. The shapes are folded onto the one canvas.     
      126 +- **The return must be used.** `circle(move px, ‚Ä¶);` alone wou
          +ld be a dead no-op. `px := circle(move px, ‚Ä¶)`                
      127 +  moves the canvas in (consuming the old binding ‚ÄĒ `own`/`move
          +` kills it), then rebinds the returned canvas                 
      128 +  with `:=`. Linear, zero-copy, fused in-place; nothing copied
          +, nothing aliased, no slice repointed.                        
      129 +- **`circles` is a fold, not a parallel `each`** ‚ÄĒ each shape 
          +consumes the previous canvas, so order matters                
      130 +  (overlap) and it can't run out of order.                    
      131 +- **No `|>`, no `frame`.** There is no value-bearing `Eff` on 
          +the draw path to `fmap` over ‚ÄĒ the pixels are                 
      132 +  pool state painted by the fold, and the **only** effect is `
          +present`/`blit` at the boundary. That keeps it                
      133 +  applicative (the fold's writes and the blit don't thread out
          +puts through each other).                                     
      134 +- **One-off** (draw + show a single circle): `painted := circl
          +e(move px, ‚Ä¶); blit(handle, move painted)()`.

‚óŹ Update(docs/design/queries-systems-and-joins.md)
  ‚éŅ ¬†Added 4 lines, removed 1 line
      49  An effect is a value. A **func builds** an `Eff` (composes effe
          cts); a **system runs** it.
      50  
      51  - An `Eff` is **run by applying its out-params with `()`**: `bu
          ild(args)(out:)`. Not with `run`.
      52 -- **`|>`** maps a **pure** func over an `Eff` (`fmap`). **`seq`
         -** sequences independent `Eff`s (applicative).                 
      52 +- **`|>`** maps a **pure** func over an `Eff` (`fmap`) ‚ÄĒ left *
         +*must be an `Eff`**, right a pure func. It is                  
      53 +  **not** a generic value-pipe: `px |> f` where `px` is plain d
         +ata is ill-typed, and a terminal effect on the                 
      54 +  right is not `fmap`. So `|>` only appears where an effect *yi
         +elds a value* (e.g. `poll()`), not on a path                   
      55 +  whose only effect is a terminal commit. **`seq`** sequences i
         +ndependent `Eff`s (applicative).

‚óŹ Done. The doc (docs/design/queries-systems-and-joins.md) and my memory now
  reflect the model as we worked it out:

  Cast ‚ÄĒ func (return must be consumed; thread with px := f(move px, ‚Ä¶)), map
  (pure parallel), each (the control-flow/effect fan; fold/scan when it threads
  an accumulator), system (never iterates ‚ÄĒ runs boundary effects only), #run
  orchestrates. proc gone, run-statement retiring.

  |> ‚ÄĒ clarified as Eff-fmap (left must be an Eff, right a pure func), not a
  value-pipe ‚ÄĒ so px |> is ill-typed and a terminal commit isn't fmap.

  Worked example rewritten to the real shape, with the each named circles (not
  the silly hardcoded "draw"):
  - Window owns the canvas (px+dims+opaque handle); Circle is just a shape.
  - circle = pure unit (paint_circle(canvas, shape) ‚Üí canvas, returns the
  canvas).
  - circles = sequential fold ‚ÄĒ px := circle(move px, ‚Ä¶) (move kills the
  binding, := rebinds; zero-copy linear thread).
  - present = the one device effect (blit via the opaque handle).
  - No |>/frame on the draw path; applicative because the pixels are pool state,
  not an effect output.

  Applicative ‚áĄ pools is written up as the load-bearing insight
  (storage-in-pools is what keeps Eff applicative; frame-as-effect was a
  smuggled monadic dependency). Plus slices-can't-repoint, FFI-opaque-only, and
  an honest "open / not yet built" list that flags the system(query) rework as
  the thing the shipped compiler still gets wrong.
